+Jamison Brereton

31 (265)
Indra
Ku┼Ыika Aiс╣г─лrathi or Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
22 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This dense and often puzzling hymn has given rise to much discussion. The heart of the hymn (vss. 4тАУ11 and passim throughout the rest of the hymn) provides one

of the fullest accounts in the R╠еgveda of the Vala myth and especially of Indra and the Aс╣Еgirases as they besiege the Vala cave and seek to free the cows within by means of song and ritual activity. Since the cows of the Vala myth are often used as symbols of the dawns, the hymn also celebrates the coming of dawn and its ritual manifestations, including the distribution of priestly gifts (dakс╣гiс╣З─Б), which occurs at the early-morning ritual.
Perhaps the most striking part of the hymn, however, is found in the first three verses, which are often taken as depicting the production of the ritual fire as an alle gory of cosmic incest. Although there are certainly hints of an incestuous liaison, the relationships among the various kinship terms here are not at all clear, and in our opinion the ritual references to the production of fire so dominate the picture and distort the underlying sexual configurations that it is a mistake to seek too literal a mythological reading. The translation of the first two verses, especially, is provisional. Our identifications of the personae with various ritual elements differ from those of other scholars (who also differ among themselves), but in our opinion the ritual reference here is not to the initial production of ritual fire, but rather the transformation, through removal to the east, of the undifferentiated ritual fire into the new offering fire, an action well known from the later ritual literature, where the new fire with its eastern hearth is called the ─Аhavan─лya and the older one in the west the G─Бrhapatya. If this particular ritual procedure was an innovation in the R╠еgveda or pre-R╠еgveda, as we suspect, a mystical and riddling presentation of it like this would not be surprising.
The connection between this opening description of the birth of Agni and the following treatment of the Vala myth may not be superficially obvious, but it is the theme of dawn that unites them: fire is kindled at dawn, and the release of the Vala cows is regularly likened to the breaking of dawn.
It is notable that neither Indra nor the Aс╣Еgirases are named for most of the recital of the Vala myth, though they are referred to constantly. Indeed the plural Aс╣Еgirases is not found in the mythic section, only the singular (vs. 7) referring to Indra. Indra is named, but not until verse 11, the exact center of the hymn (minus the refrain, vs. 22) and the standard locus for mysteries and their solutions. However, various epithets, associates, and exploits of Indra that uniquely identify him and that are irrelevant to the Vala myth have foreshadowed this naming: Saram─Б, IndraтАЩs dog, in verse 6; his opponent ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa in verse 8; and the Vr╠еtra-smashing earlier in verse 11. After the first naming of Indra in verse 11 the hymn broadens its view to include a range of IndraтАЩs cosmogonic deeds, especially the separation of Heaven and Earth and the smashing of Vr╠еtra.
The hymn returns to the ritual here-and-now starting around verse 17, and the theme of dawn, appropriate both to the fire-kindling verses 1тАУ3 and the extensive treatment of the Vala myth, prompts the requests for IndraтАЩ liberality to be mani fested in the early-morning dakс╣гiс╣З─Б, with the dispensing of gifts compared to the outpouring of cows from the opened Vala cave.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra As indicated in the published introduction, the hymn presents multiple difficulties, esp.

in its first three vss. I will not attempt to represent the many conflicting interpr. of these vss., but simply lay out some parts of my own and point to some of the many puzzles that remain. As also noted in the published introduction, I think the cosmic incest theme imposed on these vss. by others is faint at best, and also think that the ritual occasion depicted is not the original generation of the ritual fire but the removal of the ─Аhavan─лya fire from the G─Бrhapatya.

In the published introduction. I say that Indra is not named in the narrative of the Vala myth until vs. 11, but this is false: the last word of the 1st verse of the Vala treatment, 4d, is ├нndraс╕е. He is also named in the last vs. of the Vala section, 11b – thus producing a satisfying ring.

Vss. 3 to the end are tr. and discussed by H.-P. Schmidt in Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra (pp. 166-75).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe sonless father, regulating (the contract), refers to his grandson, (the son) of his daughter, and relying on the efficiency of the rite, honours (his son-in-law) with valuable gifts; the father, trusting to the impregnation of the daughter, supports himself with a tranquil mind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The sonless father: ┼Ы─Бsadvahniс╕е; the latter is said to be the father of a daughter only, not of a son, because he conveys away (vahati, pr─Бpayati) his property through his married daughter into another family; ┼Ы─Бsad, ┼Ы─Бsti, he stipulates, that this daughter’s son, his grandson, duhitur naptyam, shall be his son, a mode of affiliation recognized by law; and relying on an heir thus obtained, and one who can perform his funeral rites, he is satisfied

+Jamison Brereton

Instructing the (grand)daughter [=─Аhavan─лya?] of his daughter
[=G─Бrhapatya?], the (offering-)conveyor [=Agni] has comeтАФhe the
knowing one, ritually serving the visionary power of truthтАФ
to where the father [=priest? Agni?], stretching out straight, has run toward the outpouring of his daughter [=butter offering?] with
capable mind.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The female line of descent implied in the 1st p─Бda, duhit├║r napty├аm тАЬthe (grand)daughter of the daughter,тАЭ is striking. As noted already, I believe that this kinship succession refers to the production of the offering fire (─Аhavan─лya) from the householderтАЩs fire (G─Бrhapatya) and the removal to the east of the former. Obviously, however, this canтАЩt refer directly to the fires, because agn├н- is masc.; it is rather, I think, a reference to the hearths, which word (dhiс╣г├бn─Б- in some uses) is fem. The conveyor (v├бhniс╕е) who has come (g─Бt) is the fire itself (often called v├бhni-), which has made the journey from the G─Бrhapatya hearth to the ─Аhavan─лya hearth. The offering is being made there by the father (pit─Б╠Б), whom I take as the priest. I do not see allusion to the cosmic incest of Heaven and his daughter, in part because it is difficult to identify who the granddaughter would be. (See Oldenberg) The ritual identifications of v├бhni- = Agni and pit─Б╠Б= priest are pretty standard; it is the identity of the females that causes dispute.

+Griffith

WISE, teaching, following the thought of Order, the sonless gained a grandson from his daughter.
Fain, as a sire, to see his child prolific, he sped to meet her with an eager spirit.

+Geldner

Der Opferlenker kam die Enkelin der Tochter zurechtweisend, des Gesetzes kundig, die Erkenntnis des Gesetzes hochhaltend, wobei der Vater rechtschaffenen Sinnes einverstanden war, indem er den Ergu├Я der Tochter betrieb.

+Grassmann

Der fahrende [wie es scheint, das m├дnnliche Ileibholz, was an dem weiblichen, das hier als seine Tochter aufgefasst wird, hin und her f├дhrt], der Tochter Spross erstrebend fc┬лs in dem Sinne von ├д f┬л┬лs], ging, des Werkes kundig und die Andacht liebend, dahin, wo seine Tochter zu besamen eilend, in br├╝nstiger Gier sich mit ihr eint der Vater.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(A son) born of the body, does not transfer (paternal) wealth to a sister; he has made (her) the recptacle of the embryo of the husband; if the parents procreate children (of either sex), one is the performer of holy acts, the other is to be enriched (with gifts).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Born of the body: t─Бnvaс╕е = tanujaс╕е na j─Бmaye riktham ─Бraik, if there be a son the inheritance does not go to the sister, j─Бmaye, bhaginyai; he has made her the receptacle: and by so doing he makes her sanskс╣Ыta– he secures for her one of the essential purificatory rites; if the parents procreate children: yadi m─Бtaro janayanti vahnim: vahni = offspring, or male offspring, a son;

Avahni = a daughter; one, the son, the performer of obsequial and other rites, is the heir, while the other is rindhan, ridhyam─Бna, to be increased or made wealthy, with dresses, ornaments and the like; cf. Nirukta 3.4-6

+Jamison Brereton

The son of her body [=Agni?] has not left behind his leavings for her sister [=G─Бrhapatya?]. He has made the womb [=─Аhavan─лya?] a
repository for the winner.
When the mothers [=fingers] begot the (offering-)conveyor, one of the two good workers [=fire-churning sticks] was the actor, the other was the one assuring success.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not see sufficient evidence in this vs. for the legalistic interpr. having to do with inheritance rights advanced by Oldenberg and Geldner (fld. by Witzel Got┼Н). Again, my interpr.

involving the two fireplaces is at least thinkable, though there are a number of loose ends (in everyoneтАЩs interpr). In the first p─Бda in my interpr. the fire that has been taken out of the G─Бrhapatya leaves nothing behind. The two other occurrence of ─Бraik have womb as obj. + a dative (as if it were our p─Бda b): I.113.1 ev─Б╠Бr─Б╠Бtry uс╣г├бse y├│nim ─Бraik тАЬso night has left behind the womb for dawnтАЭ and I.124.8, which even has a sister: sv├бs─Б sv├бsre jy─Б╠Бyasyai y├│nim ─Бraik тАЬThe (one) sister has left the natal place to her older sister.тАЭ In both the idea seems to be that one has vacated the space for the other – not left as legacy, as the legalistic inheritance interpr. requires.

Problematic for my interpr. is the fact that rikth├бm should be the equivalent of the womb itself (the fireplace), not the detritus that the fire might leave in it. Moreover, the two hearths that had been daughter and granddaughter now become sisters – but a certain fluidity in modeling kinship relations would not be surprising.

In b the site of the new fire, the ─Аhavan─лya, is the womb of this new fire and тАЬthe repository of the winnerтАЭ (the winner being the fire itself).

The second half-verse is fairly clear (for this hymn) in its description of the churning of the fire: the mothers are the fingers, the two good workers are the two kindling sticks. See the fire-churning passage with kindling sticks in nearby III.29.1.

The y├бd─л opening the second half-verse is better taken as y├бd ─л, with the enclitic pronoun. See 6a below.

+Griffith

The Son left not his portion to the brother, he made a home to hold him who should gain, it.
What time his Parents gave the Priest his being, of the good pair one acted, one promoted.

+Geldner

Der leibliche Sohn hat seiner Schwester das Erbe nicht ├╝berlassen; er machte ihren Mutterleib zu einer Schatzkammer des Gewinners. Wenn die M├╝tter den Opferfahrer erzeugen, so ist einer von den beiden Gutt├дtern der Erzeuger, der andere ist der, der den Vorteil hat.

+Grassmann

Nicht ├╝berliess der Sohn [Agni, das am m├дnnlichen Reib- holze entstandene Feuer] die Erbschaft der Schwester [der am weiblichen Reibholze entstehenden Flamme]; er machte fern vom Mutterschooss sein Lager [indem er als Brennholz die Flammen des Holzstosses anz├╝ndet, und so seine Erbschaft antritt]; wenn ihn den F├дhrmann [Agni] seine Aeltern [die beiden Reibh├╢lzer] zeugen, ist von den beiden sch├╢n wirkenden der eine [das m├дnn- liche Reibholz] der zeugende, der andere [das weibliche Reibholz] der f├╢rdernde [oder gedeihende].,

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFor the worship of the resplendent (Indra), Agni, glowing with flame, has begotten mighty sons; great was the germ, and great was their birth, and great was their efficacy, for the worship of Harya┼Ыva.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Agni was begotten, quivering with his tongue [/by the offering-spoon, trembling], to display the sons [=flames?] of the great ruddy one.
Great was the womb, great the birth of these here, great the growth of the one with fallow bays [=Indra] through the sacrifices.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In the first p─Бda the instr. juhv─Б╠Аcan be read simultaneously as тАЬwith his tongue,тАЭ construed with r├йjam─Бnaс╕е and referring to the flame(s) of the fire, and as тАЬby the offering-spoon,тАЭ construed with jaj├▒e and indicating that the ghee poured from the spoon тАЬbegetsтАЭ the fire by making it flame up.

The second p─Бda is likewise ambiguous and initiates the transition to the Indra-Aс╣Еgiras-Vala myth portion of the hymn. The тАЬsons of the great ruddy oneтАЭ (mah├бs putr─Б╠Бm╠Рaruс╣г├бsya) can be the flames of the fire, that is, of Agni himself – and the infinitival pray├бkс╣гe тАШto displayтАЩ is esp. appropriate to this interpr. But they can also be, as they are identified by most commentators, the Aс╣Еgirases, the sons of Heaven, who will figure in the Vala myth about to be related, but who are also associated with Agni, who is sometimes called ├бс╣Еgirastama- (e.g., I.75.2; see Macdonell, Vedic Myth. 143). The тАЬbirth of theseтАЭ (j─Бt├бm eс╣г─Бm) in c can likewise refer to both the flames and the Aс╣Еgirases. IndraтАЩs appearance in d strengthens the Aс╣Еgiras reading and provides a transition to the next portion of the hymn.

The lexeme pr├б тИЪyakс╣г has been variously interpreted. For тАШdisplayтАЩ see Got┼Н (1st class, 153 and n. 572), EWA s.v. Curiously Witzel Got┼Н tr. it as if to тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ, despite Got┼НтАЩs own disc. just cited – though the other possibility is suggested in the n.

+Griffith

Agni was born trembling with tongue that flickered, so that the Red’s great children should be honoured.
Great is their germ, that born of them is mighty, great the Bays’ Lord’s approach through sacrifices.

+Geldner

Agni wurde mit der Zunge zitternd geboren, um die S├╢hne des gro├Яen R├╢tlichen zu verehren. Gro├Я war die Leibesfrucht, gro├Я auch diese Geburt, gro├Я die Erbauung des Falbenlenkers Indra durch die Opfer.

+Grassmann

Erzeugt ward Agni mit der Zunge zuckend, um hinzudringen zu den grossen S├╢hnen [Flammen] des feuerrothen [Agni], gross ist ihr [der S├╢hne] Spross, und gross das von ihnen geborene; durch Opfer wird gross des Flammenrosses [Agni] Wachsthum.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe victorious (Maruts) associated (with Indra when contending with Vс╣Ыtra) perceived a great light issuing from the darkness. The dawns recognizing him (as the sun) arose, and Indra was the sole sovereign of the rays (of light).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The victorious (clans [=Aс╣Еgirases?]) escorted the contender [=Indra?]. They distinguished the great light from the darkness.
Recognizing him, the dawns rose up in response. He became the lone lord [/husband] of the cowsтАФIndra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бdas a and c contain feminine plural nom./acc. forms: ja├нtr─лс╕е and j─Бnat─л╠Бс╕е тАж uс╣г─Б╠Бsaс╕е respectively. Although the default assumption would be that they are coreferential and both refer to the Dawns, the familiar plot line of the Vala myth suggests rather that they identify two different subjects: the (unexpressed) Aс╣Еgirases in ab, the (expressed) Dawns in c. (So Geldner, Renou, Schmidt [Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra, 167]; Oldenberg agrees that the Aс╣Еgirases should be supplied as subj. in a, but takes ja├нtr─лс╕е as obj. [presumably alongside clear acc. spс╣Ыdh─Бn├бm], while Witzel Got┼Н take the Dawns as subj. of a, but supply the Aс╣Еgirases as subj. of b.) The Aс╣Еgirases are IndraтАЩs back-up band in the Vala myth, as noted above ad III.30.10, and would be expected to accompany him, as p─Бda a depicts, while the Dawns are still confined within the Vala cave and only in c recognize IndraтАЩs song and come out of the cave. The problem for an Aс╣Еgiras reading of p─Бda a is of course the fem. gender of ja├нtr─лс╕е. Here it is probably best to follow S─Бyaс╣Зa. in supply v├н┼Ыaс╕е тАШclansтАЩ (so Geldner, etc.); cf. I.121.3 vi┼Ы─Б╠Бm ├бс╣Еgiras─Бm.

However, note that the Aс╣Еgirases are referred to by the fem. pl. v─Б╠Бс╣З─лс╕е тАШchoirтАЩ in the preceding hymn, III.30.10, and that noun could be supplied here. The cows of d are surely the dawns, as often; Indra becomes their p├бti-, a word meaning both тАШlordтАЩ and тАШhusbandтАЩ. On the naming of Indra here, see the introduction.

remarks above.

+Griffith

Conquering bands upon the Warrior waited: they recognized great light from out the darkness.
The conscious Dawns went forth to meet his coming, and the sole Master of the kine was Indra.

+Geldner

Dem Streiter schlossen sich die siegreichen Scharen an; sie fanden das gro├Яe Licht aus dem Dunkel heraus. Die Morgenr├╢ten erkannten ihn und kamen ihm entgegen aus der H├╢hle. Indra wurde der alleinige Besitzer der K├╝he.

+Grassmann

Die Siegerinnen [die Morgenr├╢then, als ├╝ber das Dunkel siegend] strebten hin zu dem k├дmpfenden [Agni]; sie fanden grosses Licht aus der Dunkelheit heraus; als sie ihn erblickten eilten sie hin, die Morgenr├╢then ; da ward Indra allein der Herr der K├╝he [im Vritrakampfe].

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe seven intelligent ages (the aс╣Еgirasas) having ascertained that (the cows) were concealed in the strong (cavern), propitiated (Indra) by mental devotion; they recovered them all by the path of sacrifice; for Indra, knowing (their pious acts), and offering them homage, entered (the cave).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The insightful ones bored through to the (cows), though they were in a stronghold. The seven inspired poets impelled (the cows?) with
advancing mind.
They found the whole path of truth. Himself knowing the way, he
[=Indra] entered among them [=cows] with homage.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The Aс╣Еgirases, now presumably in the masc. (though both dh─л╠Бr─Бс╕е [a] and v├нpr─Бс╕е [b] are technically ambiguous), remain the implicit subjects of abc, with Indra, also unnamed, taking this role in d. The cows, also not identified, are represented in p─Бda a by the fem. pl. part. sat─л╠Бс╕е. In fact, though these identifications are fairly easy to make for those familiar with the story, they remain covert, and, further, both b and d have unidentified objects as well. In b Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) tr. ├бhinvan without object; I have supplied the cows (so apparently also L├╝ders [Varuс╣Зa 510-11], Schmidt [Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 167]), while RenouтАЩs parenthetic тАЬ(lтАЩ)тАЭ in тАЬ(lтАЩ)incit├иrentтАЭ presumably refers to Indra.

In d there is an expressed object, but it is merely a 3rd ps. pronoun, which is, furthermore, ambiguous in sandhi: t─Б╠Бin t─Б╠Бn├бmas─Б can represent either neut. pl. t─Б╠Бor fem. pl. t─Б╠Бс╕е. The Pp. opts for the former, a decision endorsed by Oldenberg The issue is further complicated by the fact that the form could be construed with either (or both) of two verbal forms, part. praj─Бn├бn or pf. ─Б╠Бvive┼Ыa. Oldenberg takes t─Б╠Бto refer vaguely to things that Indra knows and construes it with praj─Бn├бn; sim. Renou: тАЬsachant ces choses.тАЭ Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], contra Pp., restores t─Б╠Бс╕е, which he takes to refer to pl. pathy─Б╠Ас╕е, generated from pathy─Б╠Аm in c. My tr. is closer to Schmidt and to L├╝ders, in restoring t─Б╠Бс╕е (like Geldner), but assuming its referent to be the cows, into whose company Indra enters. With L├╝ders and Schmidt, I also take praj─Бn├бn as having an implicit object inspired by pathy─Б╠Аm in c, but praj─Бn├бn is generally used absolutely to mean тАЬknowing (the way)тАЭ and so a form of pathy─Б╠А- need not be supplied. The published translation should have parentheses: тАЬknowing (the way).тАЭ

+Griffith

The sages freed them from their firmbuilt prison: the seven priests drove them forward with their spirit.
All holy Order’s pathway they discovered he, full of knowledge, shared these deeds through worship.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen Saram─Б discovered the broken (entrance) of the mountain, then Indra made great and ample (provision) for her young, as previously (promised); then the sure-footed (animal), forest recognizing their lowing, proceeded, and came to the presence of the imperishable kine.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 33.59;

Saram─Б = v─Бk, speech, that in which the gods saharamante, delight together

+Jamison Brereton

When Saram─Б found the break in the rock, she made the great ancient herd directed toward one goal.
Sure-footed, she led the vanguard of the cows [/syllables]. First
recognizing (them), she went to their bellowing.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) interpret ab as a direct quotation from the gods, for reasons that are unclear to me. Although an immediate past reading might help account for the injunctive aorists vid├бt (a) and kaс╕е (b), in fact the second hemistich also contains two injunctives, nayat (c) and g─Бt (d), the latter of which is also an aorist. So there is no clear grammatical distinction between the two half-verses, and the subject (Saram─Б) also remains the same throughout (by most interpr.), with all four p─Бdas focusing on the same narrative. Other interpreters (Renou, L├╝ders, Schmidt) ignore this odd decision of GeldnerтАЩs.

In a y├бd─л should be read y├бd ─л; see 2c above.

In b p─Б╠Бthaс╕е ordinarily means тАШfold, penтАЩ, but here refers to the herd confined in the fold: the shift from container to contained is a common one in semantic change.

├бkс╣гar─Бс╣З─Бm in c most likely has double reference, both to the cows that are being released from the Vala cave and the syllables of the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ song that effects that release.

Geldner makes the point (n. 6d) that r├бva- in this context otherwise only refers to the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩs song; this leads him to switch the subject to Uс╣гas, as the first out of the cave, coming in response to the sound of the Aс╣Еgirases. This seems, on the one hand, over-finicky – why introduce another female character in the middle of a vs. without signaling it? – and, on the other, rather deaf to the possibility of multiple meanings that always lurks in RVic discourse. One of the points of the Vala myth in general seems to me the mirroring of sounds: the song that releases the cows and their joyous counter-mooing in response – an obvious place for a poet to allow a single word to do double duty. This same double reference is found in the preceding p─Бda in ├бkс╣гar─Бс╣З─Бm. Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 167) also takes the r├бva- to be that of Indra and the Aс╣Еgirases and in fact makes Uс╣гas the subject of the whole 2nd hemistich. I do not see the need for this.

+Griffith

When Sarama had found the mountain’s fissure, that vast and ancient place she plundered thoroughly.
In the floods’ van she led them forth, light-footed: she who well knew came first unto their lowing.

+Geldner

Wenn die Sarama die Bresche imFelsen findet, so wird sie ihren fr├╝heren gro├Яen Schutz vollst├дndig machen." Die Leichtf├╝├Яige f├╝hrt die Spitze der K├╝he. Sich auskennend ging sie als erste auf den Schall zu.

+Grassmann

Als Sarama den Spalt des Felsens auffand, da bahnte sie den grossen, alten Himmelspfad, der zu einem Ziele hinf├╝hrt; mit sicherm Fuss geht sie voran; der unversieglichen [K├╝he oder Str├╢me] Get├╢n erkennend,, kam sie zuerst hin.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe most sage (Indra), desirous of the friendship of the (aс╣Еgirasas), went to the cave, and the mountain yielded its contents to the valiant (deity), aided by the youthful Maruts, equally wishing (to conciliate the sages); the destroyer (of the asuras) recovered (the cattle), and immediately aс╣Еgirasas became his worshipper.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The foremost inspired poet [=Indra] came, acting in partnership (with the Aс╣Еgirases). The rock brought the embryo to sweetness for the
good worker.
The young blood won, doing battle alongside the youths. Then he
became (an) Aс╣Еgiras immediately upon singing.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note that all p─Бdas begin with 3rd sg. preterite verbs: a ├бgachat, b ├бs┼лdayat, c sas─Б╠Бna, d (modified initial pos.) ├бth─Бbhavat (which most likely represents ├бtha abhavat, though ├бth─Б bhavat is possible). All but the perfect in c are augmented imperfects; this contrasts markedly with vs. 6, which, as was just noted, contains four 3rd sg. injunctives, three of them aorists. Three of the four p─Бdas of vs. 7 also end with nom. sg. masc. pres. participles: a sakh─лy├бn, c makhasy├бn, d ├бrcan.

P─Бda b configures the release of the cows from the Vala cave as a birth, but a birth overlaid with metaphor (тАЬbrought to sweetnessтАЭ).

In c the standard tr. (save for Renou and Klein, DGRV II.67) take makhasy├б- as тАШbeing generousтАЩ vel sim. But in all three occurrences of this verb stem (here and IX.61.27, 101.5) the тАШdo battleтАЩ sense is primary. Since it co-occurs with sas─Б╠Бna тАШwonтАЩ in this p─Бda, the тАШbattleтАЩ sense seems esp. appropriate. So Renou тАЬcomportant-encombattant.тАЭ For further on makh├б- see comm. ad I.18.9.

My tr. of d, ├бth─Бbhavad ├бс╣Еgiras─Бс╕е sady├│ ├бrcan, differs in an important way from the standard. In my opinion it states that Indra became an Aс╣Еgiras as soon as he sang; the others that the Aс╣Еgiras [=Indra] right away became a singer (e.g., Geldner тАЬDa ward sogleich der Aс╣Еgiras zum Lobs├дngerтАЭ). On the one hand, IтАЩm not certain that тИЪbh┼л + pres. part. can yield this sort of predication, esp. with the pres. part. standing in, in effect, for an agent noun. So – a syntactic argument, though I have not examined the evidence in detail. Another syntactic/lexical argument: sady├бс╕е + participle is frequently used to indicate the circumstances under which the action of the main verb takes place. This is esp. common with sady├│ j─Бt├бс╕е тАЬjust bornтАЭ / sady├│ jaj├▒─Бn├бс╕е тАЬhaving just been bornтАЭ – e.g., the next hymn, III.32.9 sady├│ y├бj j─Бt├│ ├бpibo ha s├│mam (тЙЕ10) тАЬJust born, you drank the somaтАЭ (and cf. III.29.3). But the prevailing interpr. here requires the sady├бс╕е to go with the main verb, despite its position directly before the participle – e.g., Klein тАЬAnd then did the Aс╣Еgiras straightway become a singer.тАЭ And finally a semantic objection: the proposed tr.

seems to me thematically backwards. Indra joins the category of the Aс╣Еgirases because he joins them in song, which is their principal function in this myth; he is not an Aс╣Еgiras by nature who happens to start singing. (This point is made, more or less, by Schmidt [173], despite his contrary tr.)

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay he who is the type of all that is excellent the anticipator (of his foes), he who knows all that is born, who destroys ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, the far-seeing, the restorer of cattle may he, a friend coming from heaven, honouring us as his friends, be free from all reproach.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Far-seeing: padav─лс╕е, kavitama, most wise or far-seeing as to the past, from pada, on object, and viс╕е, who knows; may he be free from all reproach: mu├▒canniravady─Бt: always, nitar─Бm, be free, mu├▒catu– from such a fault as that of the nature of the death of Vс╣Ыtra: vс╣Ыtravadhar┼лp─Бd doс╣г─Бt; the paur─Бс╣Зika notion is that Vс╣Ыtra was a brahman, and by killing him, Indra was guilty of the heinous sin of brahmahaty─Б

+Jamison Brereton

The counterweight of every being, standing at the forefront, he knows all the races; he smashes ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.
Following the track of heaven, seeking cows, chanting, the comrade released us, his comrades, from calumny.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take this vs. as a quotation of the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ praise-song of Indra.

I do not see why. The vs. seems to follow easily from the preceding one, and in fact at the end of vs. 7 itтАЩs Indra whoтАЩs singing (/chanting), not the Aс╣Еgirases. We might expect such a quotation to be signposted in some way. I do not consider the 1st pl.

enclitic naс╕е in c to be a sufficient signal.

The presence of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa in b is a bit puzzling, since the smiting of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa is not part of the Vala myth. Perhaps with Schmidt (173) he is mentioned because Indra is uncontestably ┼Ъuс╣гс╣ЗaтАЩs killer, and this extra-mythic (or extra-Vala myth) association makes it clear that the unnamed subject of this vs. must indeed be Indra.

The standard tr. take c as a separate clause from d and supply a verb of motion with pr├б (e.g., Geldner тАЬ[ging] тАж voranтАЭ). This is certainly possible, but cd can also be read as a single clause (so Schmidt, 168), since pr├б is frequent with тИЪmuc.

This interpr. allows, but does not enforce, a coreferential interpr. of naс╕е (c) and s├бkh─лn (d), as in my tr. (flg. Schmidt).

What calumny? Geldner (n. 8d) suggests the dishonor because of the loss of the herd.

+Griffith

Peer of each noble thing, yea, all excelling, all creatures doth he know, he slayeth Susna.
Our leader, fain for war, singing from heaven, as Friend he saved his lovers from dishonour.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe aс╣Еgirasas, with minds intent on their cattle, (sat down to worshipIndra) with hymns, following the road to immortality; great was their person verance by which they sought for months to accomplish (their ends).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

With cow-seeking mind, they sat down (to a ritual тАЬSessionтАЭ) with their chants, making for themselves a way toward immortality.
Just this was their long Session, by which, for months, they sought to win (the cows) through truth.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

GeldnerтАЩs suggestion that this vs. concerns the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ Sattra, a months-long ritual, seems completely convincing. Note the verb sedur тАШthey satтАЩ in p─Бda a and the nominal s├бdanam тАШsittingтАЩ in c. I am less convinced by his interpr. of c (fld. by Renou, Witzel Got┼Н), that this Sattra is frequently (bh┼л╠Бri) repeated now, though I admit that both the hic-et-nunc prn. id├бm and the particle n├║ might support his view. I prefer L├╝dersтАЩs interpr.

(Varuс╣Зa, 511, fld. by Schmidt 168), who takes bh┼л╠Бri as тАШlongтАЩ and the hemistich as a further description of the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ Sattra in the Vala myth.

My interpr. of d (based on L├╝ders and Schmidt) deviates further from Geldner (Renou, Witzel Got┼Н). All of the latter take y├йna тАж с╣Ыt├йna as coreferential and the equivalent of тАж

*с╣Ыt├бс╣Г, y├йna – that is, *с╣Ыt├бm in the main cl. as antecedent to y├йna. The main cl. *с╣Ыt├бm would be an appositive to s├бdanam тАЬthe Session, (that is,) the с╣Ыt├б by which they тАжтАЭ However, I separate the two instr. in d and take the antecedent of y├йna to be s├бdanam (тАЬthe Session by which тАжтАЭ), leaving с╣Ыt├йna to mean тАШby/through truthтАЩ as so often.

They also take m─Бs─Б╠Бn as the obj. of ├бsiс╣г─Бsan (тАЬthey sought to win the monthsтАЭ), but this acc. pl. can easily be an acc. of extent of time (again, as so often), and the true object of their desire to win can be supplied as the cows.

+Griffith

They sate them down with spirit fain for booty, making with hymns a way to life eternal.
And this is still their place of frequent session, whereby they sought to gain the months through Order.

+Geldner

Das Herz voll verlangen nach den Rindern setzten sie sich unter Lobpreisungen nieder, indem sie sich den Weg zur Unsterblichkeit bereiteten. Diese ihre Opfersitzung ist auch jetzt noch h├дufig, der rechte Brauch, durch den sie die Monate zu gewinnen suchten.

+Grassmann

Sie [die Angirasen] setzten sich nieder mit br├╝nstigem Geiste, durch Lieder sich bahnend den Weg zur Unsterblichkeit; das ist ja nun ihr grosser Wohnsitz, durch den sie nach der Ord- nung die Monate gewannen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬContemplating their own (cattle) giving milk to their former progeny (the aс╣Еgirasas) were delighted; their shouts spread through heaven and earth; they replaced the recovered kine in their plural ces, and stationed guards over the cows.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Surveying (the cows) en masse, they delighted in their own possession, milking out the milk of the age-old semen.
Their cry heated the two worlds through. Amid (all) that was born they set the outstanding one [=Indra?]; amid the cows they set heroes.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

What тАЬthe milk of the age-old semenтАЭ means is unclear to me. Geldner suggests that theyтАЩre milking their old cows, but the rhetoric seems rather overblown just to express that. L├╝ders (620-21, fld. by Schmidt 168) identifies the semen as с╣Ыt├б- and the milk as the Kultlied of the Aс╣Еgirases. This may well be, but nothing imposes this explanation, and Schmidt in fact worries briefly (173) that logically the Aс╣Еgirases should already have their Kultlied since they should have used it to free these very cows. On niс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б- тАШoutstandingтАЩ see Oldenberg, Scarlatta (648-49). The word must be derived from n├нs тИЪsth─Б, not n├н тИЪsth─Б and in fact goes literally into English as тАШstand outтАЩ, with the same idiomatic meaning. In addition to two occurrences of the simplex (this and IX.110.9), it is found in several compounds: karma-niс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б- X.80.1 a hero who stands out through his work, puruniс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б- V.1.6 (of Agni), VIII.2.9 тАШstanding out among manyтАЩ of soma. Geldner (unaccountably) takes it as тАШVerteilungтАЩ (fld. by Renou, L├╝ders 528-29, Schmidt 168), an interpr. about which Oldenberg comments rather acidly. OldenbergтАЩs own interpr.

is essentially reproduced here and was also adopted by Witzel Got┼Н.

Note the partial responsion between gh├│с╣гa in c and g├│с╣гu in d, in the same metrical position.

+Griffith

Drawing the milk of ancient seed prolific, they joyed as they beheld their own possession.
Their shout of triumph heated earth and heaven. When the kine showed, they bade the heroes rouse them.

+Geldner

Als sie die Herde ├╝berz├дhlten, freuten sie sich ihres Eigentums, indem sie die Milch des alten Samens melkten. Ihr Geschrei erhitzte beide Welten. Sie teilten sich in den Nachwuchs, sie verteilten die M├дnner auf die K├╝he.

+Grassmann

Sie freuten sich, da sie ihren Besitz [an K├╝hen] sahen, indem sie die Milch des alten Samens molken; ihr L├дrm durch- drang [wol atarad statt atapad zu lesen] beide Welten; ├╝ber das Geborene [den Nachwuchs der K├╝he ?] setzten sie einen Auf- seher, und M├дnner ├╝ber die K├╝he(?).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra,let loose the milch kine, assisted by the Maruts, born for his aid, and entitled to praises and oblations, and the excellent (cows) contributing abundantly to sacred offerings, and yielding the butter of libation, milked for him sweet (sacrificial) food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He was Vr╠еtra-smasher with (the help of) those who were born (together) [=Maruts], and he sent the ruddy (cows) surging upward with
oblations and with the chants (of the Aс╣Еgirases)тАФhe is Indra.
She of broad extent, bearing ghee-rich (milk) to him, milked out honey, sweetnessтАФthe thoroughbred cow.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of the first hemistich differs from the standard; I take it as consisting of two separate clauses, each identifying Indra in one of his most important mythic roles – in the Vс╣Ыtra-slaying and in the freeing of the Vala cows – along with his associates in those enterprises, the Maruts and the Aс╣Еgirases respectively. It is important to note that this naming of Indra, in conjunction with the first appearance of his name in 4b (see comm. there and in the introduction. remarks), frames the treatment of the Vala myth, and, by mentioning Vс╣Ыtra, it also sets the stage for the opening out of this hymn to treat other exploits of Indra.

Others take vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Бin p─Бda a simply as an auxiliary epithet of Indra in this account of the Vala myth, but I do not think that Vс╣Ыtrahan would be so promiment in a treatment of the Vala myth, and I also cannot otherwise account for the s├йd u in the middle of p─Бda a without assuming that a new clause begins there. (L├╝ders [517] gets out of this difficulty by accepting LudwigтАЩs emendation to a bahuvr─лhi sv├йduhavyaiс╕е тАШhaving sweating oblationsтАЩ [=Aс╣Еgirases], but though this is ingenious, esp. as sweat figures in the same myth in X.67.6-7 as Geldner points out, it requires too much alteration for a sequence that can make sense on its own.) In the first brief clause, vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Бis the predicate, and j─Бt├йbhiс╕е refers to the Maruts, who are well known for being тАШborn (together)тАЩ (e.g., V.55.3 s─Бk├бс╣Г j─Бt─Б╠Бс╕е). Geldner suggests, but rejects, an emendation here to saj─Бt├йbhiс╕е (for transmitted s├б j─Бt├йbhiс╕е), an idea also of AlsdorfтАЩs (see Schmidt 169); I would modify that by proposing haplology from s├б *saj─Бt├йbhiс╕е. The rest of ab concerns the Vala myth, which has been the subject of the past seven vss. The myth is readily identifiable by the VP ├║d usr├нy─Б asс╣Ыjat тАЬsent the ruddy (cows) surging upтАЭ and by the arka├нс╕е, repeated from 9a. Since the chants in 9a clearly belonged to the Aс╣Еgirases, there need not be any even oblique reference to the Aс╣Еgirases here: the bare arka├нс╕е will be enough.

+Griffith

Indra drove forth the kine, that Vrtra-slayer, while hymns of praise rose up and gifts were offered.
For him the Cow, noble and far-extending, poured pleasant juices, bringing oil and sweetness.

+Geldner

Er, der Vritrat├╢ter, lie├Я samt dem Nachwuchs, der Indra samt den Opfergaben die K├╝he durch Zauberges├дnge heraus. Die breit├дugige, h├дusliche Kuh, die f├╝r ihn die schmalzige Milch tr├дgt, hat ihren leckeren Honig aus sich melken lassen.

+Grassmann

Durch die S├╢hne [des Angiras, also durch die Angirasen ?, (S├дyana: durch die Maruts)] und durch ihre Opfer und Ges├дnge liess indra, der Vritrat├╢dter, die K├╝he heraus; ihm str├╢mte die weitreichende edle Milchkuh, welche fette S├╝ssigkeit trug, den s├╝ssen Trank zu.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey (the aс╣Еgirasas) performing pious acts made for their protector a spacious and splendid abode which they celebrated; seated (at the sacrifice) and supporting with the pillar (of the firmament) the parents (of all things heaven and earth), they established the rapid Indra on high (in heaven).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

It was for the father that they performed a ritual Session, for him also they prepared a seat, because the good workers surveyed the great, turbulent (cowpen).
Propping apart with a prop the two begetters [=Heaven and Earth], while sitting (the Session) they fixed upright the dazzling (seat).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda contains two datives, pitr├й and the prn. asmai. Because of its lack of accent, asmai cannot be a demonst. adj. with pitr├й. Geldner gets out of the difficulty by interpr. pitr├й as a simile, which allows asmai to be independently construed, but this depends on his frequent assumption that cid can be a simile marker, a role I do not think it can have. Instead I give the VP cakruс╕е s├бdanam a double reading: acdg. to the first the Aс╣Еgirases perform a Sattra for their father (see 9c), but in the 2nd they also prepare for him a literal seat. Because cakruс╕е s├бdanam participates in two clauses, each can have an independent dative, though in my opinion the datives are coreferential.

It is unclear what the referent of the object in b is, described as m├бhi tv├нс╣г─лmat тАЬgreat and turbulent.тАЭ Geldner, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa, takes it as a further reference to the seat, Renou the all-purpose тАЬquelque chose,тАЭ Schmidt the eye of the sun, Witzel Got┼Н sim. the sun-god. My own candidate is the p─Б╠Бthaс╕е of 6b, also described as m├бhi there. In vs. 6 the word is used to indicate the herd, which is contained in the fold (see comm. there); here I think it is the container, the fold or pen, itself – representing the cosmic space and also the ritual ground. When they survey it they see that this space needs organizing, which they proceed to do – by propping apart Heaven and Earth (a deed usually ascribed to Indra) and preparing and propping up a seat for Indra. They thus make the whole cosmos into IndraтАЩs ritual ground, and in the next vs. (13ab) Earth herself serves as the emplacement allowing Indra to pierce Vс╣Ыtra.

The position of the h├н is somewhat anomalous: since the whole b p─Бda forms a single clause, we would expect the h├н in WackernagelтАЩs position. However, there is a general tendency when a preverb precedes its verb late in the clause for h├н to intervene between them, as here: тАж v├н h├н khyan#. More specifically, 1) when there’s a h├н in a clause containing a verbal form of тИЪkhy─Б, it always immediately precedes the verb – sometimes in normal Wack. pos. (e.g., I.81.9), sometimes not (as here and, e.g., VI.15.15). 2) With one exception, all injunc. forms of тИЪkhy─Б are preceded either by h├н or by a preverb ending in -i, which prob. led to a sense that тИЪkhy─Б should be so preceded. Note also in this passage the phonetic echoes #m├бhi тАж vi h├н khyan#, which also resonates with p─Бda d тАж v├н minvan#. It is perhaps worth noting in this connection how many p─Бdas in this hymn begin with m├бhi or mah─л╠Б: 3d, 4b, 6b, 12b, 13a, 14a, 14c, 15a (esp. clustered here); cf. also mah├бs 3b, mah─Б╠Бn 3c, 18d. I assume that a p─Бda opening *m├бhi h├н would be avoided; in any case there are none in the RV.

In d most tr. take the sun as the referent of the object. I instead supply the seat.

The root тИЪmi often takes тАШseatтАЩ as obj.: not our s├бdanam admittedly, but s├бdmanII.15.3 (with v├н), X.20.5, I.173.3, IX.97.1, s─Б╠Бdana- X.18.13. This is a fairly large percentage of the attested forms of the verb, and since тАШseatтАЩ is already present in this vs., it is easily supplied here.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as our devout praise has appointed a thiriving ruler for the regulation of heaven and earth, to whom faultless and appropriate commendations (are due), therefore are all the energies of Indra spontaneously exerted.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

When the great (Earth), the Holy Place, has set him to piercingтАФ him who is grown strong in a single day, spread wide in the two world-halves,
and in whom the flawless hymns are unitedтАФ(then) all powers are conceded to Indra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take y├бdi here as a shortened form of y├бd *─л with enclitic pronoun (as in 2c and 6a), though it unfortunately appears before a word beginning with a single consonant. An тАЬifтАЭ makes no sense here, and it is also desirable to have an acc. pron.

in this p─Бda to serve as obj. of dh─Б╠Бt and subj. of the infinitival ┼Ыi┼Ыn├бthe. This putative

*─л may anticipate and double the heavy acc. phrase of b, assuming that the latter refers to Indra.

As noted just above, Earth herself serves as the foundation from which Indra can launch his attack. Our passage is very similar to I.102.7 … tv─Б dhiс╣г├бс╣З─Б titviс╣гe mahy, ├бdh─Б vrtr╠е ─Б╠Бс╣Зi jighnase … тАЬThe great (Earth), the Holy Place has sparked you тАж.

So you keep smashing obstacles …,тАЭ with the same mah─л╠БтАж dhiс╣г├бс╣З─Б as here and even a form of тИЪtviс╣г, like tv├нс╣г─лmat in 12b; cf. also VI.19.2 ├нndram ev├б dhiс╣г├бс╣З─Б s─Бt├бye dh─Бt тАЬThe Holy Place positioned just Indra for winning,тАЭ with тИЪdh─Б + inf. as here. The same тИЪdh─Б + inf. construction is found in 19d below: sv├а┼Ы ca naс╕е тАж s─Бt├бye dh─Бс╕е тАЬand set us up to win the sun.тАЭ Although Grassmann assigns the hapax ┼Ы├н┼Ыnathe to a them. stem ┼Ыi┼Ыn├бtha-, as Oldenberg clearly states we expect a datival infinitive here, and so it more likely belongs to an athem. stem ┼Ыi┼Ыn├бth-; cf. abhi┼Ыn├бth-.

Renou takes b as describing Vс╣Ыtra, Schmidt Indra; GeldnerтАЩs tr. is not clear, though Schmidt (169 n.) claims itтАЩs to Vс╣Ыtra. I follow Schmidt in assigning the phrase to Indra, though the poet may have intended its referent to be ambiguous, indicating that the opponents are almost evenly balanced.

I follow the current standard view (represented already by Geldner and Renou) that ├бnutta- is the ppl. to the lexeme ├бnu тИЪd─Б тАШconcedeтАЩ; Schmidt and Witzel Got┼Н follow the older deriv. from тИЪnud тАШpushтАЩ, hence тАШunpushableтАЩ vel sim.

+Griffith

What time the ample chalice had impelled him, swift waxing, vast, to pierce the earth and heaven,-
Him in whom blameless songs are all united: all powers invincible belong to Indra.

+Geldner

Wenn die hohe Disana ihn dazu bestimmt hat, den Vritra niederzusto├Яen, der an einem Tage gro├Я wurde und in beiden Welth├дlften sich breit machte, so sind alle Kr├дfte dem Indra zugestanden, auf den die fehlerlosen Lobreden sich vereinigen.

+Grassmann

Wenn die grosse mit Soma gef├╝llte Schale den schnell er- starkten Helden beider Welten zum Angriff treibt, ihn, in welchem die tadellosen Lieder sich vereinen, so sind alle ungebeugten Kr├дfte dem Indra.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWide fields, vast treasure, (spacious) pastures has the much-knowing (Indra) bestowed upon his friends; the radiant Indra with the leaders (of rites, the Maruts) genitive rated the sun, the dawn, the earth and fire.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Great the dwelling place, abundant the gleaming (goods) that he found; thereupon he assembled movable (goods [=livestock]) for his comrades.
Indra along with the men, as shining one, begot at one blow the sun, the dawn, the way, the fire.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е as the agent with the part. d─л╠Бdy─Бnaс╕е (тАЬvon den M├дnnern entflammt (?)тАЭ), but this participle never elsewhere takes an agent. Better an instr. of accompaniment, with most other tr. That Indra is described as shining may be connected to the fact that three of the four things he generates shine too: the sun, the dawn, and fire. There is some disagreement about who the men are: the Aс╣Еgirases or the Maruts. Given the general prominence of the Vala myth earlier in the hymn, but the more recent concentration on the Vс╣Ыtra myth, I imagine the ambiguity is intentional and both sets of IndraтАЩs helpers are to be thought of.

+Griffith

He, having found great, splendid, rich dominion, sent life and motion to his friends and lovers.
Indra who shone together with the Heroes begot the song, the fire, and Sun and Morning.

+Geldner

Er gewann ein gro├Яes Land, viel Gold und stellte den Freunden den beweglichen Besitz wieder her. Indra, von den M├дnnern entflammt, erzeugte miteinander Sonne, Morgenr├╢te, den Gang des Himmels, das Feuer.

+Grassmann

Einen grossen, sehr gl├дnzenden Grundbesitz ertheilend, bef├╢rderte er den Freunden recht den Fortgang; Indra erzeugte mit den M├дnnern strahlend zugleich die Sonne, die Morgenr├╢the, Wohlfahrt, Feuer.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThis lowly-minded Indra has created the wide-spread, commingled, all-delighting waters; and they, purifying the sweet (libations) with the sage purifiers, and being benevolent (to all), proceed with (the revolutions) of days and nights.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With the sage purifiers: kavibhiс╕е pavitraiс╕е = the sages, who are as it were with the filters or purifiers of the soma, are the divinities: agni, v─Бyu and s┼лrya; proceed with days and nights: dyubhir-hinvantyuktabhiс╕е = they go with days and nights, i.e. they regulate by day and night the respective functions of all the world: r─Бtridivam saravam jagat sva svavy─Бparapravanam kurvanti, they make the whole world diligent in its respective functions by night and day

+Jamison Brereton

Also the all-gleaming waters, spread wide, did this master of the house send surging forth toward a single goal.
Through the days, through the nights, (the priests) impel the runners, (the streams) of honey [=soma] being purified with poets as their purifying filters.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of this vs. differs significantly from the standard, beginning with the disposition of the p─Бdas. Most take abc together, with d as a separate clause, while I divide the vs. into two hemistichs, which express parallel notions. In ab, in mythological time, Indra sends the waters surging; this is the standard happy denouement of the Vс╣Ыtra myth. In cd priests (even perhaps the Aс╣Еgirases) impel another collection of liquid, the streams of soma – the ritual equivalent of IndraтАЩs cosmogonic release of the waters. Although the standard interpr. tacks p─Бda c onto ab, as describing the waters, it contains vocabulary that is strongly associated with soma: m├бdhu- тАШhoney, sweetтАЩ, тИЪp┼л тАШpurifyтАЩ, and pav├нtra- тАШfilterтАЩ, and I cannot offhand think of another instance in which waters are said to be purified, though they are purifying.

In ab note the return of several lexical items: vibh┼л╠Б- (13b) and sadhry├а├▒c- (6b). The cid тАШalsoтАЩ also links this vs. with a previous part of the hymn, namely 11b where Indra sends surging another group of fem. entities (ruddy [cows]): ├║d usr├нy─Б asс╣Ыjad ├нndro arka├нс╕е.

I do not understand why Indra is called d├бm┼лn─Бс╕е тАШmaster of the houseтАЩ. The word is generally an epithet of Agni (understandably), and there is nothing in this passage that seems to me to link Indra to the domestic sphere. In c m├бdhvaс╕е is taken by most as fem. acc. pl. (by Schmidt as masc. nom. pl.).

Several exx. of this form are analyzed by Grassmann as either masc. nom. pl. or fem.

nom./acc. pl. However, none of these supposed examples is convincing, and it is best to take it here as the gen. sg. it usually is. It then needs a head noun. Oldenberg adduces nearby III.36.7 m├бdhvaс╕е punanti dh─Б╠Бray─Б pav├нtraiс╕е тАЬthey purify it in a stream of honey with purifying filters,тАЭ which is very similar to our p─Бda c. I therefore supply, with Oldenberg, a form of dh─Б╠Бr─Б- тАШstreamтАЩ upon which gen. m├бdhvaс╕е depends. The precise form I supply is acc. pl. dh─Б╠Бr─Бс╕е, modified by the (fem. acc.) part. pun─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е and coreferential with dh├бnutr─лс╕е тАШrunnersтАЩ at the end of the vs. The conceit in the phrase hinvanti тАж dh├бnutr─лс╕е is that the priests are spurring on the streams of soma (like) horses. As for the subj. of hinvanti, I take it as (the current) priests (as in the sim.

passage III.36.7 just quoted; also III.46.5, where Adhvaryus are the subj. of hinvanti).

It could also be, with Renou, the Aс╣Еgirases, who have been operating as priests in the Sattra depicted earlier.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take kav├нbhiс╕е as an adjective with pav├нtraiс╕е (Geldner: тАЬmit geistigen FilternтАЭ), but in my opinion there are no adjectival uses of kav├н-. Instead it is used as a defining appositive (poets as filters), as I take it, sim. Renou, or it is a separate agent with pun─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е (тАЬbeing purified by poets with filtersтАЭ), with Schmidt (170).

+Griffith

Vast, the House-Friend, he set the waters flowing, all-lucid, widely spread, that move together.
By the wise cleansings of the meath made holy, through days, and nights they speed the swift streams onward.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe two adorable (alternations of) day and night, upholding (all things) by the might of the sun, successively revolve; your sincere and acceptable friends (the Maruts) are ready to encounter (your foes) and maintain your greatness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Day and night: the text has ubhe kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зe = both the blacks, i.e. ahor─Бtre, day and night; by the might of the sun: s┼лryasya maс╣Гhan─Б: s┼лrya = Indra, the impeller, preraka, of the world

+Jamison Brereton

The two black treasure-chambers [=Dawn and Night], deserving the sacrifice, follow (each other) in succession through the magnanimity of the Sun,
when your amiable, straight-flying comrades (gather) round about, to twist your greatness (toward them), Indra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner points out, p─Бda a is very similar to IV.48.3 ├бnu kr╠ес╣гс╣З├й v├бsudhit─л, yem─Б╠Бte vi┼Ыv├бpe┼Ыas─Б тАЬThe two black treasure chambers [=Night and Dawn], with all their ornaments, have directed themselves after each other in turn.тАЭ Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions ad III.31.17) cleverly comments, тАЬThe words kr╠ес╣гс╣З├й and v├бsudhit─л are both dvandva eka├зeс╣гa ‘black (Night) and (Uс╣гas)’ is a way of saying n├бktoс╣г─Б╠Бs─Б; conversely ’treasuregiving (Morn) and black (Night)’ is uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Бn├бkt─Б.тАЭ тАЬThe magnanimity of the sunтАЭ is a slightly surprising expression. Is it that the sun makes the succession of Night and Dawn possible by his transit across the sky, and this is considered generous on his part? Or is it an indirect reference to the distribution of the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б at dawn. A related, but opposite, sentiment is found in VII.81.4 uch├бnt─л y─Б╠Бkrс╣З╠е ├│с╣гi maс╣Гh├бn─Б mahi, prakhya├н devi sv├аr dr╠е┼Ы├й тАЬYou who in dawning make through your magnanimity the sun to be visible for seeing,тАЭ with the magnanimity credited to Dawn.

The only other occurrence of pl. с╣Ыjipy├б- (II.34.4) is at least indirectly used of the Maruts; the standard tr. all assume they are the referents of cd, which seems correct. Here they seem to be functioning as priests, attempting to bring Indra to a sacrifice.

+Griffith

To thee proceed the dark, the treasure-holders, both of them sanctified by Surya’s bounty.
The while thy ovely storming Friends, O Indra, fail to attain the measure of thy greatness.

+Geldner

Die beiden verehrungsw├╝rdigen Schatzhalterinnen, die schwarze Nacht und die Morgenr├╢te folgen ihm mit Einwilligung des Sonnengottes, w├дhrend die Freunde deine Hoheit umringen, um sie f├╝r sich in Beschlag zu nehmen, o Indra, sie die Geliebten, Vorst├╝rmenden.

+Grassmann

Es geben bereitwillig nach die beiden schwarzen, ehr- w├╝rdigen Schatzkammern der Sonne [Himmel und Erde oder Tag und Nacht, S├дy.], wenn deiner Gr├╢sse, o Indra, auszuweichen deine begehrenswerthen Genossen eilend sind.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSlayer of Vс╣Ыtra, do you, who is long lived the showerer (of benefits), the giver of food, be the lord of our true praises, repairing (to the sacrifice), come to us great, with great, friendly, and auspicious protections.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Become lord of liberalities, you smasher of Vr╠еtra, a bull of songs, conferring vigor all the life long.
Come here to us with your friendly fellowship, a great one hastening with great help.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the alliteration in b (тАж vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бyur vс╣Ыс╣гabh├│ vayodh─Б╠Бс╕е) and the rather elementary etymological figure in d (mah─Б╠Бn mah─л╠Бbhiс╕е); although sakhy├йbhiс╕е ┼Ыiv├йbhiс╕е is neither the one nor the other, it seems to function as a bridge between the two.

+Griffith

Be Lord of joyous songs, O Vrtra-slayer, Bull dear to all, who gives the power of living.
Come unto us with thine auspicious friendship, hastening, Mighty One, with mighty succours.

+Geldner

Sei du, Vritrat├╢ter, der Herr der Geschenke, sei lebensl├дnglich der befruchtende Stier der Lieder! Komm zu uns mit deinen g├╝tigen Freundschaftsdiensten, du der Gro├Яe mit deinen gro├Яen Hilfen, dich beeilend!

+Grassmann

Sei du, o Vritrat├╢dter, Herr der sch├╢nen Lieder, der Held der alles belebt und Jugendkraft verleiht; komm her zu uns mit freundlichen Genossen, als grosser du mit grossen H├╝lfen eilend.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWorshipping him with reverence, like an aс╣Еgiras, I make the ancient (Indra) renovate to accept the oblation; destroy the many impious oppressors (of your worshippers) and bestow upon us, Maghavan, yours own (wealth) for our acceptance.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Serving him with homage like the Aс╣Еgirases, I make new (their hymn) born of old, for the older one.
Run over the deceits, manifold and godless, and set us up to win the sun, bounteous one.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b, n├бvyaс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣Зomi тАж pur─Бj─Б╠Бm тАЬI make new (the hymn) born of old,тАЭ is about as succinct a summary of the RVic poetic enterprise as we can find in the text: the poetsтАЩ focus on ever new expressions based on traditional techniques and themes. In this particular case, Geldner suggests that pur─Бj├б- refers to the Preislied of the Aс╣Еgirases, about which we heard in vss. 7-8.

On the тИЪdh─Б + inf. construction, see vs. 13 above.

+Griffith

Like Angiras I honour him with worship, and renovate old song for him the Ancient.
Chase thou the many godless evil creatures, and give us, Maghavan, heaven’s light to help m.

+Geldner

Ihn ehre ich nach Art der Angiras┬┤ unter Verbeugung und mache ein vor Zeiten entstandenes Lied zu einem, das dem ├Дltesten ganz neu ist. Durchkreuze die vielen gottlosen T├╝cken und la├Я uns, du Gabenreicher, die Sonne gewinnen!

+Grassmann

Mit Anbetung ihn nach Angiras-Art verehrend, mach’ ich das alterzeugte [Lied] neu dem Alten; die vielen b├╢sen Unholdin- nen fahre ├╝ber, und lass uns, o m├дchtiger, Glanz erlangen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou purifying water have been spread abroad; fill their beds for our welfare; riding on the car, defend us from the malevolent, and make us quickly the conquerors of cattle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The far-extended mists have just become clear; carry us across to the edge of them, to well-being.
O Indra, as charioteer protect us from harm. Quickly, quickly make us winners of cows.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The mists are probably in part metaphorical – menacing threats and mental darkness – but may also refer physically to morning mists, which are clearing as the dawn sacrifice begins. Note also that p─Бda-initial m├нhaс╕е is a mirror image of m├бhi, which opens so many p─Бdas in this hymn (see comm. ad 12b).

+Griffith

Far forth are spread the purifying waters convey thou us across them unto safety.
Save us, our Charioteer, from harm, O Indra, soon, very soon, make us win spoil of cattle.

+Geldner

Die ausgebreiteten Nebel haben sich jetzt gekl├дrt, bring uns gl├╝cklich an ihr Ende! Du, Indra, der Wagenlenker, bewahre uns vor Schaden; mach uns recht bald zu Erbeutern von Rindern!

+Grassmann

Viele schw├╝le Nebel waren ausgebreitet, f├╝hre uns durch sie hindurch zum Heile, o Indra, du Wagenstreiter, sch├╝tze uns vor dem Feinde; bald, recht bald lass uns Rinder erbeuten.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, the lord of herds, has discovered the cattle, and by his radiant effulgence driven away the black (asuras), and indicating with veracity (to the aс╣Еgirasas) the honest (kine), he shut the gate uon all their own cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He shut the gate upon all: dura┼Ыca vi┼Ыv─Б av.с╣Ыс╣Зod apa sv─Бс╕е = having plural ced the cattle in the cow-pens, he covered or closed the doors, vraje g─Бс╕е sth─Бpayitv─Б t─Бni dv─Бr─Бny acch─Бditav─Бn

+Jamison Brereton

The Vr╠еtra-smasher, lord of cows, has put his cows on display. He has come between the black (nights) (and bright days) with the ruddy
manifestations (of the cows [=dawns]).
And allotting the liberalities [=gifts] in accord with truth, he opened up all the doors that are his own.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Schaeffer (Intens., 133-34) in taking the medial intens. d├йdiс╣гс╣нe in the meaning тАШdisplay (oneтАЩs own X)тАЩ – hence my different tr. of ├бdediс╣гс╣нa (a) тАШhas put on displayтАЩ and di┼Ы├бm─Бnaс╕е тАШallottingтАЩ.

I interpr. b as having a more complex construction than the standard interpr.

The trouble is the ant├бr phrase: when ant├бr governs the acc., it is only used with dual (or plurals conceived as duals – j─Бt─Б╠Бn ubh├бy─Бn [IV.2.2], e.g.), but kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бn has no overt partner here. I suggest that it is an elliptical plural-for-dual: тАЬblack (nights) and (bright days)тАЭ; cf. VIII.41.10 ┼Ыvet─Б╠Бn … kr╠ес╣гс╣З─Б╠Бn used for days and nights. The elliptical kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├й used of Night and Dawn in 17a would support this, and in 20a the clearing of the mists at daybreak (if IтАЩm right) might provide the other half of this elliptical duality. If this is correct, Indra comes between (ant├бс╕е тАж g─Бt) the nights and days with the entities appearing in the instr. (aruс╣гa├нс╕е dh─Б╠Бmabhiс╕е). aruс╣г├б- тАШruddyтАЩ can of course be used of Dawn and her various associates, esp. her тАЬcowsтАЭ; dh─Б╠Бman- is a frustratingly multivalent word, but here I think it means тАШmanifestationтАЩ vel sim, and the phrase refers to the dawns, who of course come temporally between night and full day.

The positioning of ca in d is somewhat disturbing, but I see no other way to explain it than KleinтАЩs (DGRV I.225, II.102 n. 28): it conjoins the first and second half-verses, but takes WackernagelтАЩs position in the 2nd p─Бda of the 2nd half-verse тАЬfollowing an intervening participial phrase.тАЭ sv─Б╠Бс╕е тАШhis ownтАЩ is in a very prominent position, as the last word in the last real vs. of the hymn (before the refrain, vs. 22). Why it should be emphasized that the doors that Indra opens are his own I do not know, beyond the fact that anything belonging to Indra is highly noteworthy. But I would point out that sv─Б╠Бс╕е may be a pun on s ├║ va┼Ы (s ├║ vaс╕е in pause) тАШsunтАЩ initial in 19d (though unfortunately sv─Б╠Бс╕е is not distracted here as it so often is).

+Griffith

His kine their Lord hath shown, e’en Vrtra’s slayer, through the black hosts he passed with red attendants.
Teaching us pleasant things by holy Order, to, us hath he thrown open all his portals.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe invoke for our protection the opulent Indra, distinguished in this combat, the leader in the food-bestowing (strife), hearing (our praise), terriblein battles, the destroyer of foes, the conqueror of wealth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

тАУ For blessing we would invoke bounteous Indra, most manly, at this raid, at the winning of the prize of victory,
the strong one who listens, (we would invoke) for help in battles, him who smashes obstacles, the winner of prizes.

+Griffith

Call we on Maghavan, auspicious Indra, best Hero in this fight where spoil is gathered.
The Strong who listens, who gives aid in battles, who slays the Vrtras, wins and gathers riches.

+Geldner

(╨С╨╛╨│╨░,) ╤Б╨╗╤Л╤И╨░╤Й╨╡╨│╨╛ (╨╜╨░╤Б), ╨│╤А╨╛╨╖╨╜╨╛╨│╨╛-╨┤╨╗╤П ╨┐╨╛╨┤╨┤╨╡╤А╨╢╨║╨╕ ╨▓ ╤Б╤А╨░╨╢╨╡╨╜╨╕╤П╤Е,
╨г╨▒╨╕╨▓╨░╤О╤Й╨╡╨│╨╛ ╨▓╤А╨░╨│╨╛╨▓, ╨╖╨░╨▓╨╛╨╡╨▓╤Л╨▓╨░╤О╤Й╨╡╨│╨╛ ╨╜╨░╨│╤А╨░╨┤╤Л!
